## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables sigma (stress), epsilon (strain), and T (temperature) indicate a constitutive relation for a solid under uniaxial loading with temperature-dependent stiffness, thermal strain, and possibly nonlinear elastic/plastic hardening with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved modulus–temperature dependence over a range)
- Exponential modulus softening with T: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid stiffening/softening with temperature over limited range)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Generalized thermoelastic with T-dependent stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (combined modulus change and thermal expansion effects)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (geometric/material nonlinearity at larger strains)
- Power-law hardening curve: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (empirical strain hardening/softening in monotonic loading)
- Ramberg–Osgood-like smooth nonlinearity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (captures gradual deviation from linear elasticity without explicit yield)
- Saturating/Voce-like hardening (strain saturation): sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (approach to a limiting stress with increasing strain)
- Thermally softened hardening (multiplicative separability): sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening modulated by temperature factor)
- Glass-transition-like smooth switch in stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (T - c3))) * epsilon (sigmoidal change in modulus near a transition temperature)
- WLF-style temperature shift factor (polymer viscoelastic surrogate without rate): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * (T - c2) / (T + c3)) * epsilon (strong nonlinear T-sensitivity near a reference temperature)
- Coupled nonlinear thermoelasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * T * epsilon**2 (explicit T–strain coupling beyond separable forms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma approximately proportional to epsilon; deviations suggest added epsilon**2, epsilon**3 terms.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → use multiplicative form sigma = E(T) * epsilon, where E(T) is linear/quadratic in T or smoothly varying (tanh) near transitions.
- Thermal expansion/thermal misfit → stress depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)); appears as an additive shift in the effective strain argument.
- Thermal softening of flow/strength → include a decreasing factor with T multiplying the strain-dependent part (e.g., exp(c*T) or 1/(1+exp(...)) equivalents, or tanh-based softening).
- Hardening with diminishing returns → saturating exponentials in epsilon (Voce-like) capture approach to a limiting stress at large epsilon.
- Distinct regimes (elastic vs post-yield) without explicit extra variables → approximate via smooth blends in epsilon such as tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) multiplying different slopes.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity → cross terms like T*epsilon, T*epsilon**2 indicate interaction beyond separable f(epsilon)g(T).
- Material transitions (e.g., near Tg) → sigmoidal dependence on T (tanh/logistic-like) often more physical than high-order polynomials in T over wide ranges.
